Parab 3.35. (...)


VErae divitiae non sunt opes, sed quas secum portat C^nscientia virtutes,
Bern: quae te (Reverendissime) ad plurimos (aspirante Deo) honorum gradus
evexerunt, non alia quavis open, non opum affluentia, aut Proavorum tuorum
praevalentia, de quibus inter Optimates, primos hujus Insulae incolas,
Cambro-Britannos, si qua ejusmodi sit gloria, just glorieris: Abfit invidia
verbis: Attribuas potius illud tibi Juvenalis, Tota licet veteres exornent
undique cerae
Atria: Nobilitas sola est, atque unica virtus.
Quibus ipse, et tenuitatis meae, and dignitatis tuae oblitus, solummodo
inixus, teipsum a gravissimis hujus Ecclesiae negotiis variarum misere
laborantis opinionum fluctibus, quas Deus ex bonitate sua Optimus Maximus suo
tempore reconciliet, uniatque hisce meis ausus sum literis interpellare. Ad
quem vero alium tabida oportunius confugeret tanquam ad Asylum Musa? aut
quorsum aequius haec nostra tenderet oration? Cuive potius, si quid luce dignum
tenuis haec nostra protulerit meditatio, offerrem memorabile? quam ipsi sub
excellentissimo hujus Insulae Protectore, Serus in Coelum redeat, diuque
Laetus intersit populis Britannis. Hor.


Qui primum almae Matris Oxoniensis occupat locum Academiae, a qua, tanquam e
font Pegaseo, omnes mini, quae supersunt dicendi vires (annuente Deo)
dimanarunt. Cui igitur justius divinum hoc consecrarem Poema? in usum praecipue
Cymraecorum, quam eidem, qui and eruditissimus, and incorruptissimus S.S.
Theologiae Professor, variarum linguarum, tum etiam Cambrorum valde capax,
iisque indissolubili consanguinitatis nexu conjunctus, eminer. Est quod agant
gratias Deo, quite (Doctissime) talem patriae ipsorum Patrem, and firmam
Britannicae Ecclesiae columnam constituerit.

-- Ipse semipaganus
Ad sacra vatum carmen assero nostrum, Pers.
Cui forsan liberior datur aditus, quam Authori. Digneris (Candidissime) and
spes and ratio sludiorum lucubrationes hasce nostras qualescunque sunt in bonam
accipias partem, conatibus faveas, atque Enchyridion hoc metricum sacrarum
Scripturarum Epitomen continens, in gloriam Creatoris, and publicam ipsius (un
spero) populi utilitatem, in tuam suscipias clientelam, and non tam donum, quam
donantis animum respicias obtestor.

Idem omnipotens Jehovah qui te variis virtutum ornamentis and honorum gradibus
accumulaverit, diutissime conservet incolumem, and summam utriusque vitae
couferat faeliciratem.

Tuus humilimus, In Christi Ministerio Indignissimus Servus, RI: JONESIUS.

Directions for the industrious Learner to read and pronounce the British
Language.
A, b, c, ch, d, dd, e, ff, g, ng, h, i, l, ll, m, n, o, p, ph, r, s, s, t, th,
v, u, w, y.

Whereof these following are generally of the same sound as the English, to wit,

A* b, d, ff, ng, h, l m, n, o, p, r, s, s, r.

C, as k in the English, ch like the Heb. n, ch, or the Greek.

Dd, as th, in that, then, thou etc. and not, as th in Rush, truth. etc.

G, as G in God, give, etc. and not as G, in generous, Gentiles etc.

Ll as lh.

U. i, in this, kiss, miss, etc. or e, in blew, knew, etc.

W, as oo in root, boot, etc.

Y either as u in turn, burn.

or i in third, bird* etc.

or as i in trim him, etc.

K, Q, X Z, are not (commonly) used but in foreign words, or upon some
special occasion as it is here to make up twenty different Characters.

When you have once learned to read it, you may easily come to the
understanding thereof, in few days practice and conference, as also by
perusing and comparing of the British, with the English Bible, and at your
leisure by reading of this, or the like Enchyridion.

Nil difficile volenti.

Llanfair in Chaer-Eingn^on Kalend Awst 1655.
To my Reverend, and Learned Countryman, the Author.
SIR,
IT is, among many other, one of my Imperfections, that I am not versed in my
maternal Tongue so exactly as I should be; for Languages and Words (which are
the only Creatures of Man, and the Keys of Knowledge) may be said to stick in
the memory like Nails or Pegs in a piece of Wood, which use to thrust out one
another oftentimes; yet the old British is not so driven out of me (for the
Cask still savours of the Liquor it first took in) but I can say something of
this elaborate and ingenious piece of yours, which you please to communicate
unto me so early: I cannot compare it more properly then to a basket of Poesies
gathered in the best Garden of Flowers, the Sacred Scriptures, and bound up
with such Art that every flower directs us where his Bed may be found; whence
I collect, that this work will much conduce to the advancement of (...), or
Scripture-knowledge, and consequently to the public good; it will also tend to
the honor of our whole Country, and to your own particular Repute: therefore
I wish you good success in making this child of your brain free Denizen of
the World.

James Howell.

ENCOMIASTICKS on the Author, and his Book.
To the intelligent Reader of Gemma Cambri, or The British Gemm.
1
WRite short, the Eye is pleased; speak so, the Ear
Worth weighed in both, like gold in payment; where
Much wrapped in little. This the Authors glory,
To model great things* one word is a story.
His page a Book; his line a Chapter tells.
The Reader's put to it wheth'r he reads or spells.
2
A Scrip'ure Chemist in a dramm of words,
A world of matter (and but truth) affords*
All this Isles first language; Babels sin
Confounded Tongues; but Gospel* Grace rang in
Tongues to build Sio^*numbers, weight and measure
Will cry up this Book (when once known) a Treasure
3
To Scriptures a rare Index; their high train
This went to limb in Minnums, of that strain
No Characters saw I so small; strange Skill!
To mould and shape as no man did; none will.
Were learned Andrews living, he would commend
This Tongue he studi'd, and the Book defend.
4
Those Britanns who love Scripture, read* use, look,
Next to your Bibles, make much of this Book.
Moses, ^say 42.^0.11.12.
Job, Matthew, Mark, Luke, John, Paul, Peter
You read in Prose, them may you now in Meeter:
Sing Sem'briev's, this was long foretold, the I'les
Shall praise the Lord, when Mercy on them smiles.
5
^asypodius.
Who Sun, Moon, Stars, Heavens Postures, Motions, Spheres,
Spann'd in the Clock at Strausburg* justly bears
A name of wonder; JONES does more, for He
Heavens Pandects, Canon, Code, Digests, to me
Points right, while guided by th'un-erring Clue
Of entire Scripture; I dare say, All Is True.
So short, so wondrous short, those depths to span,
'Twixt Heaven and us required more then Man.
Mi: Roberts, S.T.D. Coll^ Jesu (...)

brevis est.

Niiqui facili potuerunt ludere versu,

To the Author.
COme, come, we must be silent in thy praise,
'Cause our Encomions will but blast thy Baye,
Which Envy could not, that thou did do well,
Let thine own Verses prove thy Chronicle:
If any thee despise, he does but show
Antipathy; to wit, in daring so:
Thy fame's above his malice; that will be
Dispraise enough for him to censure thee.
Maurice Morgan.

Achrosticon.
R -- hoes duw rin i ti mor helaeth,
I -- raegori mewn Dysgeidiaeth.
C -- hrist i hun sy gannwyll i ti,
H -- wn yw ffynnon pob daioni.
A -- m die gariad i Dduw nature,
R -- hydd Christ dydi fell seren eglur.
D -- oeth a dawnus yw die lafur.
J -- 'dnabod Duw mewn mwyn-ffordd hyfryd,
O -- r blaen nid oedd gy-fryw gyfrwyddyd,
N -- i bu er ioed y fath ynghymru;
E -- dnowain lwyth a ddaeth in dysgu.
S -- ain 'r Efengyl byth a bery.

derbyn 12. mawrha 16. tal ammod 18. Paul.

TERFYN.
Datcanwn fawl ir Tad an gwnaeth,
ir Mab a ddaeth in prynnu,
ir yspryd glan an purodd ni
un Duw a thri sy'n caru.
The Authors Son's Vision.
1
BEhold! me thinks I see sad objects, all
Men-like in sable mourning clad: they call,
And say, be gone, thy aged Father's dead,
Thy patient Mother moved, with passion led,
Bewails her husbands death, her children stand
About her seven condole: put to thy hand,
Make up the eighth, and fitting things prepare
To solemnize his Funeral Rites: that are
Emblems of love, and duties to the dead,
And let him sleep a while in earthly bed.
2
Four more appear pure (of my Fathers seed,
And Mothers too) long dead, now 'live in deed,
Of shining Visage over-cloath'd in white,
With heavenly Hymns rejoicing at the sight,
As ministerial Angels, sent from high,
To guide his Soul into eternity:
Yield words of comfort to the Mourners; say
That though h^s Body's dead, intombed lay*
Yet for his worth in setting forth Gods word
In such rare form, no power of the sword,
Famine, or plague, or other chances should
Ever make his name to perish: the world would
Wear his British Gem unto the Worlds end;
As precious taken from their loving Friend:
Whereat I waked and star'd, they vanished then,
And I conceived they were but shapes of Men.
Clements Inn. ED: JONES.

Rhan or 119. Psalm.
Arglwydd gwnaethost in dda a'th was
in oll die ras in addo.
Dysg i am ddeall die air in iawn,
'r wy'n credu'n gyflawn yntho,
Cyn fy' ngostwng euthym ar gam,
in awr wife ddinam eilwaith.
Da iawn a graslawn ydwyt ti,
o dysg i mi die gyfraith.
Cystuddiwyd fi'n fawr Arglwydd da:
bywha fi'n ol d'addewyd:
Bodloner di, o Arglwydd mau,
ag offrwm genau diwyd,
Adlyd cefais, a chystudd maith:
die gyfraith yw 'nigrifwch*
Gwna i am ddeall cyfiownder gwiw
a byddaf fyw mewn heddwch.
Ath orchmynion y bywheist fi,
am hyn y rhei'ni a gofiais.
Eiddo ti wife, Duw achub fi,
die ddeddfau di a geisiais.
Tro fi rhag gweled gwagedd gwael*
bywha fi 'i gael die ffordd-di.
Cyflowna d'air a mi die was,
yna caf ras in the ofni.
Ofnais warth, o tro heibio hon,
da yw d'orchmynion tyn^r.
Well, f'a wydd in the gyfraith yw,
gwna in fyw o'th gyfiownder.
O'm genau na ddwg die air gwir,
in the farnau her yw'ngobaith.
Minnau'n wastadol cadwaf byth
die lin wehelyth gyfraith.
Datcanwn fawl etc.
